\AgdaHide{
\begin{code}%
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{module}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaModule{Prelude.Syntax}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{where}\<%
\\
%
\\[\AgdaEmptyExtraSkip]%
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{open}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{import}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaModule{Level}\<%
\\
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{open}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{import}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaModule{Function}\<%
\\
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{open}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{import}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaModule{Data.Empty}\<%
\end{code}
}

As the object language we consider simply typed $\lambda$-calculus
extended with additional features for programming with guarded recursive and coinductive
types that we call \GTT. It is a variant of Atkey and McBride's type system for
productive coprogramming \cite{atkey2013productive} with explicit
substitutions. In Atkey and
McBride's system, all judgements are indexed by a clock context,
which may contain several different clocks. They extend simply typed
$\lambda$-calculus with two additional type formers: a later modality \IC{‚ñª} for
encoding time delay into types and universal quantification over clock
variables \IC{‚àÄŒ∫} that allows them to specify coinductive types. In
\GTT, the clock context can either be empty or contain
a single clock \IC{Œ∫}.
%% We now give a description of the object type theory. This is a simple
%% type theory with guarded recursion that can be seen as a variant of
%% Atkey and McBride's type system \cite{atkey2013productive} but
%% allowing the presence of at most one clock in context.
%% In Atkey and McBride's system, judgements are parametrized by a clock
%% context. In our case, the clock context can either be empty or contain
%% a single clock \IC{Œ∫}.
\begin{code}%
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{data}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{ClockContext}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitiveType{Set}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{where}\<%
\\
\>[0][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{0}}]%
\>[2]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{ClockContext}\<%
\end{code}


%% Moreover we employ explicit substitutions, so on top of the usual we
%% define four sorts

\AgdaHide{
\begin{code}%
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{mutual}\<%
\end{code}
}


\GTT\ is a type theory with explcit substitutions. It comprises
well-formed types and contexts, well-typed terms and substitutions,
definitional equality of terms and of substitutions. All these kinds
are indexed by a clock context. We refer to types and contexts
existing in the empty clock context as \IC{‚àÖ}-types and
\IC{‚àÖ}-contexts. Similarly we talk about \IC{Œ∫}-types and
\IC{Œ∫}-contexts for types and contexts existing in the clock context
with exactly one clock \IC{Œ∫}.

\subsection{Types}

The well-formed types of \GTT\ include a unit type,
products, coproducts and function spaces. Notice that \IC{ùüô} is a
\IC{‚àÖ}-type.
\begin{AgdaAlign}
\begin{code}%
\>[0][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{1}}]%
\>[2]\AgdaKeyword{data}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{ClockContext}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitiveType{Set}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{where}\<%
\\
\>[2][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{0}}]%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{ùüô}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\<%
\\
%
\>[4]\AgdaOperator{\AgdaInductiveConstructor{\AgdaUnderscore{}‚ä†\AgdaUnderscore{}}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaInductiveConstructor{\AgdaUnderscore{}‚äû\AgdaUnderscore{}}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaInductiveConstructor{\AgdaUnderscore{}‚ü∂\AgdaUnderscore{}}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\<%
\end{code}
Similarly to Atkey and McBride's system, we include a later modality
\IC{‚ñª} as an operation on \IC{Œ∫}-types. We consider a nameless
analogue of universal clock quantification, that we call \IC{‚ñ°}
following \cite{CloustonBGB15}. The \IC{‚ñ°} modality takes a
\IC{Œ∫}-type and returns a \IC{‚àÖ}-type. The well-formed types \GTT\
include a weakening type former \IC{‚áë}, which embeds \IC{‚àÖ}-types into
\IC{Œ∫}-types.
%% In addition to the usual simple type formers, there are types that
%% allow us to specify guarded recursive and coinductive types. We have
%% the later modality, which takes a type in the \IC{Œ∫} clock context and
%% returns a type in the \IC{Œ∫} clock context.
%% We have clock quantification, which takes a type in the \IC{Œ∫} clock
%% context and returns a type in the \IC{‚àÖ} clock context. 
\begin{code}%
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚ñª}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\<%
\\
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚ñ°}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\<%
\\
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚áë}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\<%
\end{code}
Guarded recursive types are defined using a least fixpoint
type former \IC{Œº}.
\begin{code}%
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œº}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Poly}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\<%
\end{code}
\end{AgdaAlign}
For the \IC{Œº} operation to be well-defined, one typically limits
its applicabiility to strictly positive functors. We instead consider
a functor grammar \F{Poly} \Ar{Œî} which includes codes for constant functors,
the identity functor, products, coproducts and the later modality.
The presence of the constructor \IC{‚àÅ} for representing the code of constant functors forces the type family
\F{Poly} to be defined simultaneously with \F{Type}.
%% The type \F{Poly} \Ar{Œî} specifies a grammar for functors we allow 
%% The constructor \IC{Œº} takes an element of \F{Poly} and returnA guarded recursive type in a clock context \Ar{Œî} takes an element of
%% \F{Poly} \Ar{Œî} as its input. We call these elements polynomials.

The constructors of \F{Poly} \Ar{Œî} suffice for the specification of interesting examples of guarded recursive types such as streams. Nevertheless it would not be complicated to add exponentials with
constant domain and the box modality to the grammar, but we leave this as a future effort.
We associate to each code \Ar{P} in \F{Poly} \Ar{Œî} a functor \F{evalP}
\Ar{P} acting on \F{Type} \Ar{Œî} defined by induction on \Ar{P}.
\begin{code}%
\>[0]\AgdaFunction{evalP}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%

\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\<%
\end{code}
%% Then \IC{Œº} \Ar{P} is then the least fixed point of \F{evalP} \Ar{P}. Notice that for this kind of fixed points to exist, one typically restricts the constructors of
%% the type family \F{Poly} so that the functor \F{evalP} \Ar{P} is
%% strictly positive, for all \Ar{P}.  Here we consider a grammar for
%% polynomials consisting of constant functors, the identity functor,

%% constant domain and clock quantification could also be added to the
%% grammar, but we did not consider them in our formalization.

\AgdaBound{Y}\<%

\AgdaBound{X}\AgdaSpace{}%

\AgdaBound{X}\<%

\subsection{Contexts}
The well-formed contexts of \GTT\ include the empty context, context extension and context weakening. The last operation embeds \IC{‚àÖ}-contexts into \IC{Œ∫}-contexts.
\begin{AgdaAlign}
\begin{code}%

\\
\>[0][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{0}}]%
\>[2]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚Ä¢}\AgdaSpace{}%

\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Context}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\<%
\\
%
\>[2]\AgdaOperator{\AgdaInductiveConstructor{\AgdaUnderscore{},\AgdaUnderscore{}}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%

\AgdaInductiveConstructor{Œ∫}\<%

%% In addition to the usual context formers, we have context
%% weakening. This operation takes a context in the \IC{‚àÖ} clock context
%% and returns a context in the \IC{Œ∫} clock context. It is the context
%% analogue of the type former \IC{‚áë}. Notice that we are overloading the

\subsection{Terms}

The well-typed terms and substitutions of \GTT\ are defined simultaneously. Terms
include constructors for variables and substitutions.

The later modality is required to be an applicative functor and this is evindenced by the terms \IC{next} and \IC{‚äõ}. The fixed point combinator \IC{fix-tm} allows the specification of productive recursive programs.

We have introduction and elimination
rules for the \IC{‚ñ°} modality. The rule \IC{box-q} is the analogue in \GTT\ of 
Atkey and McBride's rule for clock abstraction
\cite{atkey2013productive}. Notice that \IC{box-q} can only be applied
to terms of type \Ar{A} over a weakened context \IC{‚áë}
\Ar{Œì}. This is in analogy with Atkey and McBride's side condition
requiring the universally quantified clock variable to not appear free
in the context \Ar{Œì}. Similarly, the rule \IC{unbox-q} corresponds to
clock application. The operation \IC{force} is used for removing occurrences of \IC{‚ñª} protected by the \IC{‚ñ°} modality.

We have introduction and elimination rules for type weakening:
elements of \F{Term} \Ar{Œì A} can be embedded in \F{Term} (\IC{‚áë}
\Ar{Œì}) (\IC{‚áë} \Ar{A}) and vice versa.

\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Context}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚áë}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSymbol{)}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚áë}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSymbol{)}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\<%
\end{code}
Atkey and McBride assume the existence of certain type equalities
\cite{atkey2013productive}. M{\o}gelberg, working in a dependently typed setting, consider similar type isomorphisms \cite{Mogelberg14}. In \GTT\ we
follow the second approach. This means that we do not introduce an
equivalence relation on types specifying which types should be
considered equal, as in Chapman's type theory
\cite{Chapman09}. Instead, we include additional term constructors
corresponding to functions underlying the required type
isomorphisms. For example, the clock irrevelance axiom formulated in our setting states that every \IC{‚àÖ}-type \Ar{A} is isomorphic to \IC{‚ñ°} (\IC{‚áë} \Ar{A}). This is obtained by adding a constructor \IC{‚ñ°const}.
\begin{code}%
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚ñ°const}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Context}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚àÖ}\AgdaSymbol{)}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚ñ°}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{(}\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚áë}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSymbol{)}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚ü∂}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSymbol{)}\<%
\end{code}
It is possible to construct an element \F{const‚ñ°} in \F{Term} \Ar{Œì}
(\Ar{A} \IC{‚ü∂} \IC{‚ñ°} (\IC{‚áë} \Ar{A})). In the definitional equality on terms, we
ask for \IC{‚ñ°const} and \F{const‚ñ°} to be each other inverses.
We proceed similarly with the other type isomoprhisms.

\subsection{Substitutions}
For explicit substitutions we consider canonical necessary operations \cite{AltenkirchK16,Chapman09}: identity and composition of
substitution, the empty substitution, the extension with an additional term and the projection which forgets the last term.

We add a rule embedding substitutions between \IC{‚àÖ}-contexts into substitutions between \IC{Œ∫} contexts and vice versa.
context.
\begin{code}%
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{weakenS}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%

\AgdaBound{Œì‚ÇÇ}\AgdaSymbol{)}\<%
\end{code}
\NV{We need to add an inverse to weakenS, in analogy with the ‚á° and ‚Üì term constructors.}
We require contexts to satisfy two isomorphisms: \IC{‚áë ‚Ä¢} needs
to be isomorphic to \IC{‚Ä¢} and \IC{‚áë} (\Ar{Œì} \IC{,} \Ar{A})
needs to be isomorphic to \IC{‚áë} \Ar{Œì} \IC{,} \IC{‚áë}
\Ar{A}. We add two constructors corresponding to functions underlying
the context isomorphisms:
\begin{code}%
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{‚Ä¢{-}to{-}weaken}\AgdaSpace{}%

It is possible to define an element \F{weaken-to-‚Ä¢} in \F{Subst}
(\IC{‚áë ‚Ä¢}) \IC{‚Ä¢}.In the definitional
equality on substitutions, we ask for \IC{‚Ä¢-to-weaken} and
\F{weaken-to-‚Ä¢} to be each other inverses. We proceed similarly with
\IC{,-weaken}.

subst{-}Œº{-}help : ‚àÄ \{Œî\} (Œì : Context Œî) (A B : Type Œî)
  ‚Üí Subst (Œì , (A ‚ä† B)) (Œì , A)
subst{-}Œº{-}help = \{!!\}

weaken{-}evalP : \{Œì : Context ‚àÖ\} (P : Poly ‚àÖ) (A : Type ‚àÖ)
  ‚Üí Term (‚áë Œì) (‚áë (evalP P A) ‚ü∂ evalP (weakenP P) (‚áë A))
weaken{-}evalP \{Œì\} P A = lambdaTm (sub (varTm (‚áë Œì) \AgdaUnderscore{}) \{!!\})

weakenŒº : (P : Poly ‚àÖ) ‚Üí Term ‚Ä¢ (Œº (weakenP P) ‚ü∂ ‚áë (Œº P))
weakenŒº P =
  primrec (weakenP P)
          (lambdaTm (sub (‚á° (cons P (varTm ‚Ä¢ \AgdaUnderscore{})))
                         ((,{-}weaken ‚Ä¢ (evalP P (Œº P)) o
                           (weakenSA (‚áë (evalP P (Œº P))) ‚Ä¢{-}to{-}weaken o
                           \{!!\})) o
                           subst{-}Œº{-}help ‚Ä¢ (evalP (weakenP P) (Œº (weakenP P))) (evalP (weakenP P) (‚áë (Œº P))))))
{-}\}}\<%

\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{infix}\AgdaSpace{}%

\subsection{Definitional equalities}
Definitional equalities on terms and substitutions are defined simultaneously.
Here we only discuss equality on terms, we refer to the Agda formalization for the equality on substitutions.
\AgdaHide{
\begin{code}%
\>[0]\AgdaKeyword{mutual}\<%
\end{code}
}
\begin{AgdaAlign}
\begin{code}%
\>[0][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{1}}]%
\>[2]\AgdaKeyword{data}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaDatatype{\AgdaUnderscore{}‚àº\AgdaUnderscore{}}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Context}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaPrimitiveType{Set}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaKeyword{where}\<%
\end{code}
The term equality includes rules for equivalence, congruence and
substitution. There are also $\beta$ and $\eta$ rules for the type
former. Among these rules, here we only show the ones associated to the
\IC{‚ñ°} modality. The rules state that \IC{box-q} and \IC{unbox-q} are each
other inverses.
%up to \AD{‚àº}.
\AgdaHide{
\begin{code}%
\>[2][@{}l@{\AgdaIndent{1}}]%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{refl‚àº}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚àÄ}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Context}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Type}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œî}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{\{}\AgdaBound{t}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{:}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaDatatype{Term}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{Œì}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{A}\AgdaSymbol{\}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaSymbol{‚Üí}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{t}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaOperator{\AgdaDatatype{‚àº}}\AgdaSpace{}%
\AgdaBound{t}\<%
\\
%
\>[4]\AgdaInductiveConstructor{sym‚àº}\AgdaSpace{}%

There are rules exibiting that \IC{‚ñª}, \IC{next} and \IC{‚äõ} satisfy the applicative functor laws. The fixpoint combinator \IC{fix-tm} must satisfy its characteristic unfolding equation.
%% There is also the
%% characteristic equality of the fixpoint combinator, stating that
%% \IC{fix-tm} \Ar{f} is equal to the application of the function term
%% \Ar{f} to \IC{next} (\IC{fix-tm} \Ar{f}).
We refer to M{\o}gelberg's paper \cite{Mogelberg14} for a complete list of equalities that the later modality and the terms associated with it are required to satisfy.

There is a group of term equalities exibiting the existence of
certain type isomorphisms. For example, we have equalities stating
that \IC{‚ñ°const} and \F{const‚ñ°} are each other inverses.
\begin{code}%
%

\NV{Here we are using app-map, which we haven't introduced in the paper.}
The last group of term equalities describes the relationship between the
weakening operations \IC{‚á°} and \IC{‚Üì} and other term constructors. Here we omit the description of these rules and we refer the
interested reader to the Agda formalization.
